<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000775"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>A very long lived and interesting plant, the<a href="http://www.namibweb.com/welwitschia.htm">Welwitschia</a>.  Found only in the Namib desert, it reverses the water absorption cycle.  Unlike most plants, which draw in water from the roots, transport it up the stem, and then out through stroma in the leaves, this plant absorbs moisture from fog in the air and transmits it through the rest of the plant.  Can live at least 2000 years.  A relation to the conifers.  Has only two leaves.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000775.html">12:53 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=775" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000774"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>From <a href="http://www.ccp4.ac.uk/newsletter41/02_ccp4i-oct02/ccp4i-oct2002.html">here</a>.</p>

<p>Automating Tasks</p>

<p>Two trial initiatives for automating tasks within CCP4i are included in 1.3.8, both of which involve passing information via XML files.<br />
Parameter passing in Molecular Replacement </p>

<p>Background: before running the Molrep task it is useful to know certain details such as the number of monomers expected in the unit cell, and the existance of pseudotranslation vectors. These can be determined using the ``Cell Content Analysis'' and ``Analyse MR Data'' tasks respectively from the Molecular Replacement module, but in each case the data must be manually transfered from the log files to the Molrep interface.</p>

<p>In this pilot project, both the ``Cell Content Analysis'' and ``Analyse MR Data'' tasks generate XML output files recording key information. These files are generated by calls to the CCP4 XML-writing library PXXML within the MATTHEWS_COEFF and PEAKMAX programs, activated using the XMLOUT keyword in each.</p>

<p>The Molrep task can then automatically check for the existence of these output files and use the information in them to fill out the appropriate fields in the task interface for the user, reducing manual handling and typographical errors.</p>

<p>Reading of the XML files is performed using a set of utility functions built upon xml.tcl 1.9 and sgml.tcl 1.7, both included in CCP4i 1.3.8. (Note that the XML output of ``Cell Content Analysis'' has to be processed, with the number of monomers used being estimated as that number giving a solvent fraction closest to 50% of the unit cell.)</p>

<p>This option is turned off by default in CCP4i 1.3.8. Users wishing to try it can switch on the functionality in the ``XML Output'' folder in their ``Preferences'' (accessed from the menu on the RHS of the main window).<br />
CAD AutoReindexing </p>

<p>Background: occasionally when merging together MTZ files using CAD, it is possible that some will have different indexing conventions to the others leading to errors when combining them.</p>

<p>The CAD task now includes the option to ``Automatically check and enforce consistent indexing between files''. With this option selected each MTZ file is checked for consistent indexing against the first file, which is used as a reference. Files which are differently indexed are then reindexed prior to being merged. This mechanism cuts down on the overhead of manually diagnosing and correcting such cases when they arise.</p>

<p>This option uses XML passing within a single task rather than between tasks, as in the previous example. In this case ALMN is used to diagnose whether reindexing is required between two files, and if so then which reindexing operator to use. This information is written to a temporary XML file using the same mechanism as before, and is read from within the script using Tcl XML utilties.</p>

<p>In both these examples it would also have been possible to pass the same information using other mechanisms, for example by processing the log files directly using a variant on ``grep'' and other Unix-type cutting-and-sorting tools. However such methods are usually overly-complicated and prone to being easily broken by even small changes to log file formats. In contrast XML parameter passing is far simpler, more robust and easily extensible.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000774.html">12:19 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=774" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (5)</a>
	
	
</div>

<h2 class="date">november 28, 2003</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000942"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p><a href="http://weekly.ahram.org.eg/2003/665/bo3.htm">Excellent article by Umberto Eco</a> - On organic, vegetal and mineral memory.  This talk was given at the new Alexandria Library.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000942.html">05:21 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=942" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000941"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Two cute grep commands for protein structures in .pdb files:</p>

<p><b>1) Count the number of residues in a .pdb file</b><br />
For this one, I strongly suggest using the first command with "less" first, to make sure there aren't any weirdly named waters or other co-factors.  If there are, just add them to the "grep -v" section.</p>

<p>Explanation:<br />
First, we remove the REMARK card.  Then we grep for an ATOM or HETATOM (hetero-atom) card.  Then, we cut out both the residue name and number (it's important to get the residue number as well, as you could have two or more residues in a row with the same name.  Then we remove any "WAT or HOH" (water molecules).  Then, we use uniq, which makes a list of just the uniq lines.  Then we count up all the lines.  Simple.</p>

<pre>
grep -v REMARK filename.pdb | grep "ATOM\|HETATM" | cut -b18-26 | grep -v "WAT\|HOH" | uniq | less
grep -v REMARK filename.pdb | grep "ATOM\|HETATM" | cut -b18-26 | grep -v "WAT\|HOH" | uniq | wc -l
</pre>

<p><b>Count the number of each type of atom in a .pdb file</b><br />
This one is a lot simpler, just cut out the atom type field, sort them and use uniq with the -c flag, to count all the occurences.  Neat. <br />
<pre><br />
grep "^ATOM\|^HETATM" 1e3m.pdb | cut -c13-14 | sort | uniq -c<br />
</pre></p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000941.html">11:27 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=941" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<h2 class="date">december 23, 2003</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000992"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>ARP/wARP errors</p>

<p>I got the following error in ARP/wARP:</p>

<pre>
cp: cannot stat `/home/sness/Paper/arp-warp-all/arp_warp_runs/haptbrSHARP/1_mir_model_1.pdb': No such file or directory
grep: arp_0.pdb: No such file or directory
grep: arp_0.pdb: No such file or directory
 Refmac_5.1.24:  No Scatterers

<p></pre></p>

<p>This was due to an error in the ARP/wARP scripts where MAPMASK was making the wrong sized maps.  You can fix this by changing the <b>xyzlim</b> keyword in the ARP/wARP .par (parameter) file.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000992.html">01:28 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=992" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>If you bake bread with the wheat that grows on my grave<br />
you'll become drunk with joy and<br />
even the oven will recite ecstatic poems.<br />
If you come to pay your respects<br />
even my gravestone will invite you to dance<br />
so don't come without your drum.<br />
Don't be sad. You have come to God's feast.<br />
Even death cannot stop my yearning<br />
for the sweet kiss of my love.<br />
Tear my shroud and wear it as a shirt,<br />
the door will open and you'll hear<br />
the music of your soul fill the air.<br />
I am created from the ecstasy of love and<br />
when I die, my essence will be released<br />
like the scent of crushed rose petals.<br />
My soul wants to leap and join<br />
the towering soul of Shams.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
-- Translation by Azima Melita Kolin<br />
and Maryam Mafi<br />
"Rumi: Hidden Music"<br />
HarperCollins Publishers Ltd, 2001<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000983"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>If you get the following error when running Solomon:</p>

<pre>
 Non Primitive Spacegroup of order   2
 FCS Multiplied by   2
                                                                                                                                                               
 Check map header agrees with fixed requirements for SFcalc for this  spacegroup.
 Check Nxyz     180 196 204    180 196 204
                                                                                                                                                               
 Check map header agrees with fixed requirements for SFcalc for this  spacegroup.
 Check Iuvw       0   0   0      3   1   2
 SFALL:   **** Fatal disagreement between input info and map header
Times: User:       0.1s System:    0.0s Elapsed:     0:00
>>>>>> CCP4 library signal ccp4_general:Cannot find input file (Success)
     raised in ccp4setenv <<<<<<
</pre>

<p>It's because your map has the slow, intermediate, fast sections in the wrong order.  One way to fix this is to use SFTOOLS to read your map in and output it in the correct order:</p>

<pre>
sftools
mapin input.map
mapout output.map order c a b
</pre>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000983.html">10:59 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=983" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000963"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Excerpt from Sri Shastriji at Siddhashram Schweibenalp, May 10, 1985<br />
(full text at www.babaji.net in the 'who is shastriji' section, then Shastriji's Speeches link)<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
The change of the heart can change kranti (revolution) into shanti (peace). As great scientists are working every minute of their waking hours to create<br />
nuclear and other weapons to destroy mankind, the same way you should be partaking in this great effort of repeating "Om Namaha Shivaya" or any other great mantra that you want to recite, and with this force, change the course of annihilation into peace. For spiritual strength is much greater, thousands of times greater, than material might. Sri Mahaprabhuji appeared to us for the benefit of mankind, to give all the good mankind was lacking. He wanted harmony and for mankind to be one family, only that there should be no class or caste distinctions. He wanted all the world to live together I harmony.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
Every country, all nations should be brothers. There should be no distinctions between colors, black, or white, or yellow. Everybody in harmony, unitedly, enjoying this beautiful creation of the Lord. As you all have gathered here and are doing this beautiful job in this most beautiful place, the same way, spread the message of Sri Mahaprabhuji, of truth, simplicity and love to the maximum amount of people, to all corners of the world and start gathering together in harmony, in peace, in love and truth and simplicity, to live in that manner and unite the world as one big family. At the end of every speech Sri Mahaprabhuji always used to say, "Be fearless and the moment that you become fearless, nothing on this earth can touch you. No catastrophe, no other adverse force can touch you!"<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
BHOLE BABA KI JAI!<br />
JAI MAHA MAYA KI JAI!<br />
JAI MAHAPRABHUJI KI JAI!<br />
JAI VISHWA!<br />
*****************************<br />
Truth**Simplicity**Love<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000963.html">12:19 pm</a>

<p>pdb-mode.el to the rescue!  I needed to renumber the atom serial numbers in a .pdb file that I had.  I tried looking, found PDBSET in the CCP4, but this doesn't do serial number renumbering.  </p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000959"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>  The purpose of nama japa is to help focus the mind on<br />
the Divine.  Frequent repetition of the mantra focuses one's<br />
mind more and more on The Divine and other unnecessary, distracting thoughts<br />
are crowded out.  So a mantra helps focus<br />
the mind in two ways - toward the Divine and away from the "trash"<br />
that often accumulates in our minds and clutters up our mental computer<br />
discs.  Who cares what witty response you might have made to the put-down at<br />
last nights's party, and how long do remember the dreams you spin as you go<br />
to work?  How many hours a day are our minds half-focused on the<br />
mind-chatter"?<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
  Lord Krishna, in the Bagavad Gita, told Arjuna,"...you must remember me at<br />
all times and do your duty.  If your mind and heart<br />
are set on me constantly, you will come to Me. Never doubt<br />
this." Isaiah commented on the power of this focus on the Divine<br />
in these words:  "Thou wilt keep him in perfect peace, whose mind<br />
is stayed on thee, because he trusteth in thee."<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
Taken from<br />
I am Harmony<br />
by Radhe Shyam<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000959.html">04:31 pm</a>

<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Prosveta Publishing is pleased to offer you the Daily Meditation for this 2003-12-07.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
"Try to get rid of this bad habit that consists in protecting the memory of all that has made you suffer: you carry this memory around with you, scrutinise<br />
it, and mull it over...It is dangerous to return to negative events in this way. Once and for all you should draw useful conclusions from them for the future<br />
and never return to them. Why do you still aggravate and prolong the ills you have suffered? Instead, try to remember the most luminous moments of your life;<br />
reflect on how, and thanks to whom, they came about. Bring them often to mind, exactly as you play the music you love, and you will re-live the same<br />
sensations of purity, freedom, and light. "<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
Omraam Mikhal Avanhov<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000951"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Ok, another very cute find command.  This is using my mtzcat program, a very simple CCP4 C-library based program to act like cat for these binary reflection files, used in macromolecular crystallography:</p>

<pre>
fwnc0200 1548 [~/Paper/data/dna] % find . -name '*mtz' -printf "%20f\t" -exec mtzcat -n {} \;
      dna90paper.mtz    Number of Reflections: 4157
 dorota_long_360.mtz    Number of Reflections: 4281
  dorota_long_90.mtz    Number of Reflections: 4253
       final_dna.mtz    Number of Reflections: 16102
     dna360paper.mtz    Number of Reflections: 4276
    dorota_short.mtz    Number of Reflections: 16102
     dna360tests.mtz    Number of Reflections: 16123
      dna90tests.mtz    Number of Reflections: 16120
      acendna360.mtz    Number of Reflections: 3361
       acendna90.mtz    Number of Reflections: 3258
</pre>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000951.html">03:33 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=951" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>

<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>  "(An) attribute of perfection is justice and impartiality.<br />
This means to have no regard for one's own personal<br />
benefits and selfish advantages, and to carry out the<br />
laws of God without the slightest concern for anything else.<br />
It means to see one's self as only one of the servants of God, the<br />
All-Possessing, and except for aspiring to spiritual distinction,<br />
never attempting to be singled out form others.  It means to<br />
consider the welfare of the community as one's own.  It means, in brief to<br />
regard humanity as a single individual, and one's own self<br />
as a member of that corporeal from, and to know of a certainty that<br />
if pain and injury afflicts any member of that body, it must inevitably<br />
result in suffering for all the rest."<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
"Abdu-'l-Baha"<br />
The Secret of Divine Civilization<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
Note:<br />
Abdu-'l Baha was considered a Master<br />
of the Baha i faith. His father was Baha u llah.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="000944"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Ok, here's a very useful little change to make to the xemacs list-mode.el source file:</p>

<pre>
;              (frame-width (or (last-nonminibuf-frame)
;                   (selected-frame)))
; sness
               (window-width (get-lru-window (last-nonminibuf-frame)))
</pre>

<p>Comment out the first two lines and add the last line.  This solves a very annoying bug when using Xemacs in tty mode with a C-x 3 vertically split screen.  The bug is that when you do completion in this split window, the contents are created before the window is created, and if the window isn't as wide as the frame, part of the window will be truncated.  This hides some of the filenames that you're looking for, and is quite irritating.  </p>

<p>I found this great patch on the web <a href="http://list-archive.xemacs.org/xemacs-beta/200009/msg00137.html">here</a>.  It looks like it might be going into the beta xemacs 21.5. </p>

<p>Hopefully all of this verbosity will help google find this page for you, dear reader, with a variety of search terms.  Bon chance. </p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/000944.html">11:32 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=944" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (7)</a>
	
	
</div>
